--- Commit Message ---
LU-8130 osc: convert osc_quota hash to xarray

The cl_quota_hash originally had 3 hashes, one for each type of quota
(USR, GRP, PRJ) that just stored on the client whether a particular
quota ID was over its limit. This was overkill since cl_quota_hash
only needs one bit to check if a particular ID has exceeded quota
with IO from this client, and there will usually be only a few IDs
that are actually exceeding their limit where a client is involved.
Instead, use the quota ID as the index into an Xarray, and store
a value with the quota TYPE(s) that are over the limit for that ID.
We only need to test the presence/absence of an ID and a quota type
without the need to store any additional values (the clients do not
track the actual quota usage or limits).
To test if a quota is exceeded for particular ID is a two-step
process. First check if there is any entry for the particular ID,
and if it exists then check which quota type (USR, GRP, PRJ) is
over the limit for that ID value.  The same is done when setting
a particular quota ID/TYPE is over its limit - first lookup the
ID and then add the TYPE flag to the value if not already set.
The Xarray implementation does offer using "marks" (up to 3 bits
per index) but in this case there is no other value that needs to
be stored into the Xarray other than one bit for any exceeded type,
so they are not used here.

--- Message (Neil Brown, 2019-05-30 00:57:55.000000000) ---
Patch Set 25:

I like the simplicity of this, but I think it is racy.
When checking if a bit is set, you set it, and then maybe clear it.
If another thread checks the same bit at the same time, it might see that it is set, when it shouldn't.  This could lead to false quota errors. 
However often is this lookup called?  Setting and clearing bits at high frequency would not be a good idea.

I think that, longer term, we do want to use xarray directly.  However, think backporting that for older kernels would be a bad idea, so ida might be best for now - if it can be made to work without races and without high frequency updates.

--- Message (James Simmons, 2020-03-13 17:37:46.000000000) ---
Patch Set 26:

Now that the Xarray patch is in better shape the question is how to implement this.  We could keep the kmem cache and allocate for each id (uid,gid,projid) and then use xa_set_mark() to distinguish each type. That means only one allocation is needed for each type of id.

The other approach is use xa_mk_value() and store it in the Xarray. This avoids needing a memory cache but we need 3 separate Xarrays for each type.

What do you think the best approach is?

Patch Set 51:

I'm stumped by that Janitor crash.
The trace shown is the last one rather than the first, which is a bit confusing.
The first crash is a list manipulating bug-check in page_cache radix-tree code.  Now changes you have made should affect that.

It is also as though the xa code is messing with the internal radix-tree code, which is weird.
Maybe if the radixtree memcache is being shared with the xa memcache, and if one corrupts something, that might cause a problem.  But as they both have a constructor function, they cannot possibly be shared.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2023-08-25 05:32:19.000000000) ---
Patch Set 71: Code-Review-1

(2 comments)

I'm not convinced that this is actually working properly by having all quota types in the same array, or if that actually saves any memory over having three separate arrays.

--- Message (Timothy Day, 2023-08-25 13:54:50.000000000) ---
Patch Set 71:

From my understanding, the goal of the code is to answer "Is gid/uid/projid xyz over quota?".

https://git.whamcloud.com/?p=fs/lustre-release.git;a=blob;f=lustre/osc/osc_cache.c;hb=2a498f06ccc975fb57214961db6e20a6c1cc2ec7#l2301

So we just need to independently set/unset a bool for each gid/uid/projid. With Xarray, we have:

 [id] -> [gid_bit, uid_bit, projid_bit]

which should be enough to store all of the info we need. The Xarray maps the id to a pointer. In this case, the pointer is fake - it's really an unsigned long - with certain bits used as bools. This is independent of Xarray marks, which is another way of tagging Xarray entries which can be used regardless of what's in the Xarray. Those are limited to 3.

This scheme should work regardless of the name or quota limit. The actual space accounting is handled elsewhere.
